Confederated Salish & Kootenai Tribes v. Clinch


No. 97-609


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 342; 297 Mont. 448; 992 P.2d 244; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 346; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 1356


January 7, 1999, Argued, Submitted  
December 30, 1999, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners requested that the court accept original jurisdiction and issue an order or other appropriate writ enjoining respondents from issuing water use permits on petitioners' reservation until such a time as their water rights have been quantified.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner Indian tribes had water rights on their reservation. Respondents asserted they had authority under Mont. Code Ann. § 85-2-311 to issue water use permits on the reservation. The court held that it could exercise original jurisdiction over the issue since petitioners demonstrated that tribal water rights were of statewide importance, and since the decisive issue was purely constitutional and the normal litigation process was inadequate. Petitioners possessed reserved water rights on the reservation pursuant to Mont. Const. art. IX, § 3(1), which they were attempting to quantify. The court construed the statute to mean respondents could only issue permits with respect to legally available water. Legally available water did not include water reserved for Indian tribes. Respondents could not determine whether the water was legally available on petitioners' reservation because they could not determine whether the issuance of permits would affect existing water rights until petitioners' rights were quantified.


OUTCOME: The court exercised original jurisdiction since petitioners established that the issue was of statewide importance and purely constitutional, and the normal litigation procedure was inadequate. Respondents were enjoined from issuing permits until petitioners' water rights were quantified since respondents could not determine whether the permit would affect petitioners' existing water rights.

 

2 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. Luchau


No. 99-345


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 336; 297 Mont. 415; 992 P.2d 840; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 349; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 1340


October 14, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
December 29, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, The Honorable John W. Larson, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the ruling of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, County of Missoula (Montana), finding the statute making it a crime for a person under the age of 21 to operate a motor vehicle while having an alcohol concentration of .02 or more constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with operating a motor vehicle while having an alcohol concentration of .02 or more while under the age of 21 in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-410. Appellant argued the statute was unconstitutional and entered a conditional guilty plea and appealed. On appeal, the court found that the offense was a strict liability crime and did not contain an unconstitutional presumption. Also, the court found that the statute did not violate appellant's equal protection rights, nor did the statute require a finding of harmful result. Consequently, the judgment finding the statute constitutional was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment ruling the statute constitutional was affirmed, because the crime was one of strict liability without elements and containing no presumptions.

 

3 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Estate of McCarthy v. Montana Second Judicial Dist. Court


No. 98-651


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 309; 297 Mont. 212; 994 P.2d 1090; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 314; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 1241


March 23, 1999, Argued; March 25, 1999, Submitted  
December 9, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied March 16, 2000. Released for Publication March 16, 2000.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded for entry of an order granting summary judgment to the Estate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner estate applied for a writ of supervisory control seeking relief from the order of the Second Judicial District Court, Silver Bow County (Montana), in a medical malpractice action, denying petitioner's motion for summary judgment which sought dismissal claiming the action was barred by the applicable statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The estate of a doctor sued for medical malpractice moved to dismiss because the action was time barred. The trial court denied the motion, holding Mont. Code Ann § 27-2-205(2) unconstitutional as violative of the right to access to the courts guaranteed by Mont. Const. art. II, § 16, and the right to equal protection of the laws guaranteed by Mont. Const. art. II, § 4. The court reversed, holding that that the classification of minors in Mont. Code Ann. § 27-2-205(2) was rationally related to a legitimate legislative objective, passed the rational basis test, and did not violate Mont. Const. art. II § 16, and that the statute, which allowed the period of limitations for certain minors to run when they reach their eighth birthday, did not violate the right to equal protection of the laws guaranteed by Mont. Const. art. II, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, and directed entry of summary judgment for petitioner, concluding that the classification of minors in the applicable statute of limitation was rationally related to a legitimate legislative objective, and that the statute did not violate the state's guarantee of right to access to the courts.

 

4 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Thayer v. Uninsured Employers' Fund


No. 99-002


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 304; 297 Mont. 179; 991 P.2d 447; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 318; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 1223


August 12, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
December 7, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 22, 1999. Released for Publication December 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: Workers Compensation Court, State of Montana. The Honorable Mike McCarter, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Workers' Compensation Court, State of Montana, concluding the Uninsured Employers' Fund properly terminated petitioner's benefits and that Mont. Code Ann. § 39-71-511 did not violate Mont. Const. art. II, § 16.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's husband died as a result of injuries received while at work. His employer was uninsured, so respondent Uninsured Employers' Fund paid decedent's medical expenses, and paid her monthly workers' compensation death benefits. Petitioner sued her husband's employer, a co-employee, and other third parties, alleging various theories of liability in connection with her husband's death. After she settled that lawsuit, respondent setoff the settlement amount against the future monthly workers' compensation death benefits payable to petitioner, resulting in termination of those benefits. She sued respondent challenging the termination of benefits and the constitutionality of the statute allowing the setoff. The Workers' Compensation Court concluded that respondent's termination of benefits was proper and upheld the constitutionality of the statute. The supreme court affirmed the judgment holding respondent was not an insurer, and therefore was entitled to a setoff against third-party recovery.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment holding that the Uninsured Employers' Fund was not an insurer; therefore, it was entitled to a setoff against recovery from third-parties and to terminate petitioner's benefits. Court also held that statute allowing the setoff was constitutional.

 

5 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Dahl v. Fred Meyer, Inc.


No. 98-632


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 285; 297 Mont. 28; 993 P.2d 6; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 302; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 1149; 15 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1376; 139 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,793


April 22, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
November 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and for the County of Flathead, The Honorable Ted O. Lympus, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the order confirming an arbitration award and dismissing plaintiff's claims of wrongful discharge against defendant with prejudice from the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District of the State of Montana, Flathead County.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant for wrongful discharge. Plaintiff alleged that defendant's motive for the discharge was that his fringe benefits were greater than those of other workers with the same annual earnings. The parties ultimately agreed to arbitration. The arbitrator dismissed on the grounds that the Employee Retirement Income Security Act (ERISA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 1001, et seq., required exclusive federal court jurisdiction. The district court confirmed and denied plaintiff's request to amend to remove the motive allegations. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that plaintiff waived his right to object on appeal by failing to object either at arbitration or in district court on the issue of ERISA preemption, and that the district court lost jurisdiction to allow plaintiff to amend the complaint when the parties agreed to arbitration. Once the parties agreed to arbitration, the district court could only confirm, modify and confirm, or vacate and remand for rehearing.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed dismissing arbitration and denying plaintiff's request to amend because plaintiff waived his right to object on appeal by failing to object below and district court was without jurisdiction to allow amendment once parties agreed to arbitration.

 

6 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. Quiroz


No. 99-066


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 270N; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 280


October 21, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
November 4, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION, THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in table case format at: 1999 Mont. LEXIS 593.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Sixteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Powder River, The Honorable Gary L. Day, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment and sentence of Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Powder River County (Montana) after jury verdict finding him guilty of misdemeanor offense of violating a protective order under Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-626(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the "harass or annoy" language in the protective order that he was convicted of violating was unconstitutionally vague. The court concluded that defendant waived his right to raise this issue on appeal because a passing reference to the issue in his trial court brief did not give the trial court an opportunity to correct any errors and did not properly preserve the issue. As a result, defendant's conviction for violating the protective order would stand. The court declined to address defendant's challenge to the separation requirement in the protective order as an unconstitutional infringement of his right to travel because the trial court's sentence and judgment were affirmable based on the court's conclusion that defendant's conviction of the protection order was valid.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because defendant did not preserve issue of unconstitutional vagueness of protective order before trial court, thus waiving issue on appeal; court declined to address constitutional right to travel issue because case could be resolved on other grounds.

 

7 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Montanans for the Responsible Use of the School Trust v. State ex rel. Bd. of Land Comm'rs


No. 98-535


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 263; 296 Mont. 402; 989 P.2d 800; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 277; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 1065


May 18, 1999, Argued; May 27, 1999, Submitted  
November 2, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.
Subsequent appeal at Montanans v. Darkenwald, 2005 MT 190, 2005 Mont. LEXIS 347 (Aug. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, The Honorable Dorothy McCarter, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Montana Board of Land Commissioners and Department of Natural Resources and Conservation appealed and plaintiff citizens' action group cross-appealed a decision of the District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark (Montana) regarding the constitutionality of various school trust lands statutes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff citizens' action group challenged 14 school trust lands statutes. The trial court permanently enjoined 11 statutes. On appeal the court held Mont. Code Ann. § 77-1-130 unconstitutional because it required use of 1972 values rather than full market value for school trust land right-of-way purchase. The rental policy under Mont. Code Ann. § 77-1-208 did not violate the full market value trust requirement. In authorizing firewood permits without charges for commercially valuable wood on school trust lands, Mont. Code Ann. § 77-5-211 unconstitutionally violated the trust mandate and the State's undivided loyalty duty. Mont. Code Ann. § 77-6-304 was facially unconstitutional because it violated the undivided loyalty duty, benefiting third parties to the detriment of the trust's beneficiaries. Mont. Code Ann. § 77-6-305 was facially unconstitutional since it did not allow a new lease to issue until the old lessee had been paid for his improvements. The lower court denial of attorney fees resulted in substantial injustice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings because various school trust lands statutes were facially unconstitutional since they violated the full market value trust requirement and state's undivided loyalty duty by benefiting third parties to the detriment of the trust's beneficiaries.

 

8 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Armstrong v. State


No. 98-066


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 261; 296 Mont. 361; 989 P.2d 364; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 272; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 1045


October 15, 1998, Heard; July 1, 1999, Submitted  
October 26, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, The Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State appealed the District Court of the First Judicial District, County of Lewis and Clark's (Montana) grant of plaintiff medical professionals' motion for a preliminary injunction in suit which sought a determination that Mont. Code Ann. §§ 37-20-103 and 50-20-109 violated the privacy provisions of the Montana Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff clinic, physicians, and physician assistants-certified filed suit, challenging the constitutionality of Mont. Code Ann. §§ 37-20-103 and 50-20-109, which prohibited physician assistants-certified from performing abortions. After it found that plaintiffs had standing to challenge the statute on behalf of female patients, the court ruled that the right of privacy was a fundamental right, and, as such, applied a strict-scrutiny analysis. The court held that the statutes violated the right to privacy under Mont. Const. art. II, § 10, because the statutes were a disguised attempt to limit patient access to a pre-viability abortion, and the legislation was not justified by a compelling state interest. The fundamental right to personal and procreative autonomy and to individual privacy prohibits the government from dictating, approving, or condemning values, beliefs, and matters ultimately involving individual conscience, where opinions about the nature of such values and beliefs are seriously divided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of plaintiffs' motion for a preliminary injunction and determined the case on its merits. A statute which prohibited physician assistants-certified from performing abortions violated the privacy, equal protection, and bill of attainder provisions of the Montana Constitution because there lacked a compelling state interest.

Montana Envtl. Info. Ctr. v. Department of Envtl. Quality


No. 97-455


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 248; 296 Mont. 207; 988 P.2d 1236; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 266; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 964; 49 ERC (BNA) 1402


September 10, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
October 20, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 28, 1999. As Corrected October 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, The Honorable Jeffrey Sherlock, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff environmental groups appealed from the District Court of the First Judicial District's (Montana) holding that absent a finding of actual injury, Mont. Code Ann. § § 75-5-317(2)(j) (1995) was not unconstitutional as applied, and entry of judgment in favor of defendant Department of Environmental Quality.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff environmental groups alleged that defendant Department of Environmental Quality illegally amended intervenor's mineral exploration license to allow discharge of groundwater containing high levels of arsenic and zinc into river aquifers, without requiring nondegradation review pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 75-5-303(3) (1995). Plaintiffs alleged that to the extent that intervenor was authorized to do so under Mont. Code Ann. to § 75-5-31(2)(j) (1995), the statute violated the fundamental right to a "clean and healthy" environment guaranteed by Mont. Const. art. II, § 3, and the nondegradation policy established by Mont. Const. art. IX, § 1. The trial court held that the statute was not unconstitutional as applied. On appeal, the judgment was reversed. To the extent the statute excluded activities from nondegradation review without regard to the nature or volume of the substances being discharged, it violated a fundamental state constitutional right providing for a "clean and healthful" environment.


OUTCOME: Judgment holding that a water quality statute was not unconstitutional as applied was reversed. To the extent the statute excluded activities from nondegradation review without regard to the nature or volume of the substances being discharged, it violated a fundamental state constitutional right providing for a "clean and healthful" environment.

Kiser v. Department of Revenue


No. 99-253


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 228; 296 Mont. 93; 987 P.2d 363; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 234; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 897


August 5, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
September 28, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, Honorable Thomas C. Honzel, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the District Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who applied for the same beer/wine license as respondent, but whose application was denied, appealed from the order of the District Court of the First Judicial District, in and for the County of Lewis and Clark (Montana), affirming the issuance of a retail beer/wine license to respondent.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, who had applied for liquor license, appealed the lower court's order affirming the department of revenue's (DOR's) decision to award a beer/wine license to respondent, contending that the decision was not supported by substantial evidence, and the DOR hearing examiner erred in finding the respondent cafe was the applicant best able to satisfy public convenience and necessity, in that the petitioner would be able to supply more liquor to more people for more hours per day than respondent.. The court rejected petitioner's view of public convenience and necessity, and affirmed, holding that the lower court's findings of fact were not clearly erroneous, and the DOR's decision awarding the subject license to respondent was supported by substantial evidence and was not otherwise clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the district court affirmed, because the lower court's findings of fact were not clearly erroneous, and the decision awarding the subject license to respondent was supported by substantial evidence and was not otherwise clearly erroneous.

 

11 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neill


No. 99-029


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 224; 296 Mont. 71; 985 P.2d 154; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 230; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 886


August 5, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
September 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Yellowstone, The Honorable Susan P. Watters, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant youth appealed judgment of the District Court, Thirteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Yellowstone (Montana) based on denial of due process under U. S. Const., amend XIV, when, without hearing, the court allowed the state to file an information pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-206.


OVERVIEW: Defendant youth appealed judgment which allowed the state to file an information theft pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-206 alleging he committed felony burglary and felony, without first affording defendant a hearing. The dispositive issue on appeal was whether the trial court violated defendant's right to due process of law, under U. S. Const. amend XIV. The court held that because the seriousness of the crime and the interests of community protection required the information be filed in district court, absent the opportunity provided by a hearing to challenge the prosecution's allegations of probable cause, defendant did not receive the due process to which he was entitled. Judgment reversed and case remanded for further proceedings. Court further held that a prior ruling to this effect which occurred subsequent to judgment could be applied retroactively to defendant because case his pending on direct review and not yet final when the earlier case was decided.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded for further proceedings; the crime's seriousness and the community's interests required the information be filed in district court, absent the opportunity provided by a hearing to challenge the prosecution's allegations of probable cause, the youth did not receive the due process to which he was entitled.

 

12 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Cusenbary v. Mortensen


No. 98-345


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 221; 296 Mont. 25; 987 P.2d 351; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 231; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 864


February 11, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
September 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, The Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the jury's verdict and the judgment of the District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of District Court of Eighth Judicial District, in and for County of Cascade (Montana), in which jury returned verdict against defendant in amount of $ 750,000 in plaintiff's action against defendant for serving a patron alcohol immediately prior to an automobile accident that caused plaintiff's injuries.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured when an intoxicated tavern patron drove a vehicle through the wall of the tavern. Plaintiff sued defendant, the tavern owner, for the injuries, claiming that the tavern's employees negligently served intoxicating liquors and alcoholic beverages to the patron when he was already visibly intoxicated. The jury returned a verdict against defendant in the amount of $ 750,000. On appeal, the court affirmed the verdict and the judgment, because the patron's conduct of driving a vehicle while intoxicated, through the wall of the tavern, was a foreseeable intervening cause that did not serve to supersede or break the causal chain between defendant's original negligence and the injury to plaintiff. The trial court did not err in excluding evidence of criminal proceedings against the patron or in allowing testimony regarding an estimate of the patron's blood alcohol concentration. The trial court properly dismissed defendant's third party complaint.


OUTCOME: Verdict and judgment affirmed, because patron's conduct of driving a vehicle while intoxicated, through the wall of the tavern, was a foreseeable intervening cause that did not serve to supersede or break the causal chain between defendant's original negligence and the injury to plaintiff.

 

13 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bedwell


No. 98-549


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 206; 295 Mont. 476; 985 P.2d 150; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 214; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 805


May 13, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
September 9, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, The Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged judgment of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial Circuit, Cascade County (Montana), which dismissed information seeking to charge respondent as an adult for burglary.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to respondent's burglary arrest, appellant petitioned for removal of the charge from youth court to trial court. Trial court granted leave to file the charge, but dismissed the charge upon respondent's motion arguing the removal statute violated constitutional separation of powers doctrine. According to respondent, the statutes granting removal powers accorded the judicial branch with powers reserved for the executive branch. Respondent also contended that removal violated his due process rights. Court first held that the removal statutes at issue were jurisdictional in nature, as they afforded trial court the right to exercise discretional jurisdiction over certain charges. Thus, court held the statute did not violate separation of powers doctrine. Court then held that, provided a hearing was held to determine whether to grant leave for appellant to file the charge, respondent's due process rights would not be violated. However, as no such hearing was held, court vacated the order granting leave and remanded for trial court to order a hearing on appellant's motion.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and remanded for a hearing on whether to grant leave to appellant to file information charging respondent as an adult.

State v. Webb


No. 98-566


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 190N; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 197


July 22, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
August 10, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION, THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in table case format at: 1999 Mont. LEXIS 375.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Musselshell, The Honorable Roy C. Rodeghiero, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourteenth Judicial District (Montana) convicting him of two misdemeanor driving offenses and imposing sentence. Defendant appeared pro se, asserting that he was not guilty of either charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on two misdemeanor driving offenses and sentence was imposed by the court. Appearing pro se, defendant appealed the convictions, asserting that he was not guilty of either charge. The court affirmed the convictions. The court noted that Mont. R. App. P. 23(a)(4) requires an appellant's opening brief to set forth the contentions being made with respect to the issues presented and the reasons therefor, together with citations to the authorities, statutes and pages of the record relied on. However, defendant's brief in several instances did not point to a specific jurisdictional problem or ruling by the court which he contended was erroneous. Consequently, the court refused to address most of defendants' claims since he did not follow appellate rules of procedure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions because defendant failed to establish a record sufficient to enable it to rule upon the issues raised.

 

15 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Department of Corrections v. Lake County (In re J.A.)


No. 97-659


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 148; 295 Mont. 46; 983 P.2d 327; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 155; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 585


September 17, 1998, Argued; October 20, 1998, Submitted  
June 29, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, In and for the County of Lake, The Honorable C. B. McNeil, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: The order of the District Court requiring that DOC reimburse Lake County for its costs incurred transporting J.A. to the San Marcos facility in Texas is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Corrections challenged the order of the District Court of the 20th Judicial District, In and for the County of Lake (Montana), which required appellant to reimburse appellee county for its costs incurred in transporting a committed youth to an out-of-state treatment facility. Appellant claimed that Mont. Code Ann. § 52-5-109 was not unconstitutional and was not an unfunded mandate that violated Mont. Code Ann. § 1-2-116.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Department of Corrections refused to comply with the district court's order requiring it to pay the cost of transporting a committed youth to an out-of-state treatment facility, and, thus, appellee county paid the costs. Later, the district court ordered appellant to reimburse appellee for those costs. The district court held that the portion of Mont. Code Ann. § 52-5-109, which directed the district court to arrange for the transportation of committed youth was unconstitutional and that appellant's attempt to shift the transporting costs to appellee violated Mont. Code Ann. § 1-2-116(2)(a). On appeal, the court held that § 52-5-109 was constitutional, as it did not encroach upon judicial authority, require the judiciary to exercise executive power, or interfere with internal judicial operations. Thus, in view of the constitutionality of § 52-5-109, appellant had not violated § 1-2-116(2)(a). The court, however, affirmed the decision that appellant reimburse appellee for its transporting costs. Under § 52-5-119, appellee was only required to pay for the transportation of committed youth within the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision requiring appellant to reimburse appellee for the cost of transporting the committed youth in question to an out-of-state facility. Although it was not unconstitutional to require the district court to arrange for the transportation of committed youth, appellee was required to pay for the transportation of committed youth only within the state.

 

16 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Balyeat Law, P.C. v. Harrison


No. 98-028


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 144; 295 Mont. 13; 983 P.2d 902; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 153; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 566


January 28, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
June 18, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, The Honorable Douglas G. Harkin, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband and appellant wife challenged the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula (Montana), which ordered them to pay medical bills to respondent trustee.


OVERVIEW: Respondent filed a complaint against appellants that sought payment for medical care provided to the appellants' children. A trial court heard the case without a jury and dismissed the case. Respondent appealed to a district court. Appellants moved for a jury trial. The district court denied this request, reasoning that appellants waived their right to a jury trial by failing to request a jury at the trial court level. The district court ruled in favor of respondent and ordered the appellants to pay respondent. Appellants challenged this decision. The appellate court first held that respondent was the proper party to bring the complaint because there was a valid trust agreement between respondent and the hospital which cared for the children. However, the appellate court further held that there was a right to a trial by jury in appeals from lower court proceedings. Therefore, the district court erred in concluding that appellants waived their right to a jury trial. The appellate court reversed the judgment and remanded for a de novo trial by jury in the district court.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment that ordered appellants to pay medical bills to respondent trustee was reversed because appellants were improperly denied their right to a jury trial. The case was remanded to the district court for a jury trial.

 

17 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. Renee


No. 97-698


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 135; 294 Mont. 527; 983 P.2d 893; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 145; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 545


January 28, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
June 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Yellowstone, The Honorable Diane G. Barz, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A criminal defendant sought review of a sentence imposed by the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone (Montana), after defendant pleaded guilty to three misdemeanor offenses, two of which were reduced from felony charges for robbery in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-201(1) and for intimidation in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-203.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged consecutive jail terms imposed after he pleaded guilty to three misdemeanors, two of which were reduced from felony charges for robbery and intimidation. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by refusing to consider sentencing alternatives available to nonviolent felony offenders under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-201(11), because the statutory term "nonviolent felony offender" did not encompass misdemeanor offenders such as defendant. Thus, plaintiff was ineligible for alternative sentencing under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-225. These sentencing statutes did not unconstitutionally deprive misdemeanants of their due process and equal protection rights because the classes "felons" and "misdemeanants" were not similarly situated. By choosing to plead guilty to misdemeanors, defendant voluntarily removed himself from the class of nonviolent felons to whom the legislature intended to offer prison alternatives. The court affirmed defendant's prison sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's prison sentences imposed after he pleaded guilty to three misdemeanors, two of which were reduced from felonies; by voluntarily pleading to misdemeanors, defendant removed himself from the class "nonviolent felony offenders" that was eligible for alternative sentencing possibilities.

 

18 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Henry v. State Compensation Ins. Fund


No. 98-351


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 126; 294 Mont. 449; 982 P.2d 456; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 128; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 506


February 18, 1999, Heard; February 19, 1999, Submitted  
June 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: Workers' Compensation Court State of Montana The Honorable Mike McCarter, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Workers' Compensation Court is reversed and this case is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker sought review of the judgment of the Workers' Compensation Court (Montana) after it denied him vocational rehabilitation benefits. The issue before the court was whether the Occupational Disease Act violated the equal protection clause of the Montana Constitution to the extent that it failed to provide vocational rehabilitation benefits to diseased workers.


OVERVIEW: Appellant worker who was injured on the job and suffered a herniated disk was denied vocational rehabilitation under the Occupation Disease Act (ODA), even though it was provided to injured workers under the Workers' Compensation Act (WCA). Appellant's claim was treated and accepted as an occupational disease. The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the lower court. The court held the ODA violated the equal protection clause of the Montana Constitution because it failed to provide vocational rehabilitation benefits to diseased workers. The court held that providing rehabilitation benefits to workers covered by the WCA, but not to workers covered by the ODA, was not rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest of returning workers to work as soon as possible after they had suffered a work-related injury.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment was reversed and remanded. The court held that providing rehabilitation benefits to workers covered by the Workers' Compensation Act, but not to workers covered by the Occupational Disease Act violated the equal protection clause of the Montana Constitution to the extent that it failed to provide vocational rehabilitation benefits to injured workers.

 

19 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spina


No. 97-240


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 113; 294 Mont. 367; 982 P.2d 421; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 130; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 467


January 28, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
May 27, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: Youth Court and District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Judge Presiding (Youth Court).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed a judgment from the Youth Court and District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, Cascade County (Montana), convicting her of negligent homicide. Defendant urged that she should not have been tried a an adult and that the transfer provisions of Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-206 violated her right to equal protection under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the Mont. Const. art. II, § 4.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial of defendant as an adult and her conviction and sentence for homicide. The findings of fact and conclusions of law in the youth court's transfer order were not in error. There was probable cause to believe that defendant committed the homicide, that treatment was required beyond that afforded by juvenile facilities, and that defendant acted in an aggressive, violent, or premeditated manner. Therefore, the youth court did not abuse its discretion in waiving its jurisdiction. The transfer provisions of Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-206 (statute) did not violate defendant's rights to equal protection under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the Mont. Const. art. II, § 4. The waiver of jurisdiction was not predicated on the state's inability to find a juvenile system placement but because the duration of and post-release supervision for such a placement would be insufficient. The statute did not require defendant's psychological evaluation without a waiver of her constitutional rights. The issue of whether such a waiver was obtained was not reviewed because it was first raised on appeal. Claims that publicity deprived defendant of a fair trial were unsupported.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the waiver of youth court jurisdiction, defendant's conviction for negligent homicide, and the sentence. The court concluded that the transfer provisions of the statute were constitutionally sound and that there was no abuse of discretion in the transfer of defendant's case to the district court.

State v. McCarthy


No. 98-238


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 99; 294 Mont. 270; 980 P.2d 629; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 112; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 418


April 8, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
May 18, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin, Honorable Mike Salvagni, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Gallatin (Montana), which convicted defendant of stalking a victim by mail.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for stalking his wife, who had obtained a temporary restraining order against him. Defendant had telephoned and mailed letters to his wife, and was convicted of violating the protective order, but sent two letters to her from prison. Two unwanted contacts were sufficient to establish the element of repeated contact. There was sufficient evidence to show that defendant's wife suffered substantial emotional distress or reasonable apprehension of bodily injury or death, because the many letters defendant sent her prior to his first conviction had contained threats, and because her relationship with defendant had been tumultuous. The court did not have to decide whether Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-220 was constitutionally void for vagueness or for overbreadth, because the argument was not raised before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for stalking because two unwanted attempts at contact with defendant constituted repeated instances, and because the circumstances and the history of the relationship showed the element of emotional distress. Constitutional claims did not have to be considered because they had been raised below.

Hawkins v. Mahoney


No. 98-168


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 82; 294 Mont. 124; 979 P.2d 697; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 88; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 345



April 20, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 3, 1999. Released for Publication June 3, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 06/03/1999


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Hawkins, 165 Mont. 456, 529 P.2d 1377, 1974 Mont. LEXIS 440 (Mont., 1974)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for postconviction relief in an original proceeding, seeking review of his first-degree murder conviction and sentence of life imprisonment on the grounds of ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to life imprisonment for the shooting death of his wife. Defendant's first petition for postconviction relief was denied by the trial court, which defendant failed to appeal. Subsequently, the trial court summarily dismissed defendant's second petition on the basis that defendant failed to attach the required affidavits and factual documents and that the ineffective assistance of counsel issues were resolved in the prior proceeding. Thereafter, defendant petitioned for postconviction relief in an original proceeding. The court denied the third petition, holding that it was time barred under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-102 (1991) and a successive petition under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-105(1) (1995). The court applied the five-year limitations period, which was the statute in effect at the time the petition was filed, rather than the statute in effect at the time of conviction. Further, the miscarriage of justice exception to the limitations period did not apply where defendant failed to allege newly discovered evidence. Thus, the petition, which was filed more than 20 years after defendant's conviction, was time barred.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for postconviction relief, finding that the petition was time barred where it was filed beyond the five-year statute of limitations period in effect at the time defendant's petition was filed and that the petition was barred as a successive petition.

 

22 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. Butler


No. 98-134


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 70; 294 Mont. 17; 977 P.2d 1000; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 73; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 291


October 29, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
April 6, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Second Judicial District, In and for the County of Silver Bow, The Honorable James E. Purcell, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his judgment of conviction by the Second Judicial District Court, Silver Bow County (Montana), which denied his motion to declare Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-206 (1997) unconstitutional for violating his due process rights by allowing the prosecution to file an information directly in district court rather than youth court without first affording him a hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 16 years old. He was charged with attempted deliberate homicide and attempted robbery. Defendant moved to declare Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-206 (1997) unconstitutional because it violated his due process rights by allowing the prosecution to file an information directly in district court rather than in youth court without first giving him a hearing. The district court denied defendant's motion and entered a judgment of conviction based on his guilty pleas. Defendant appealed and the court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction. The court held that the district court violated defendant's right to due process as guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, when it allowed the prosecution to file an information in district court under § 41-5-206 of the Youth Court Act, without first affording him a hearing. There was no need, however, to declare the entire provision unconstitutional as defendant requested. Instead, the court simply held that due process required the district court to hold a hearing when rendering a decision under § 41-5-206(3).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and remanded because the Fourteenth Amendment guaranteed defendant juvenile a right to a hearing before allowing the prosecution to file an information in district court.

State v. Worrall


No. 98-282


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, for the County of Chouteau (Montana), which denied his motion to suppress certain evidence. Thereafter, defendant pled guilty to the offense of criminal manufacture of dangerous drugs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by information with the criminal production or manufacture of dangerous drugs, criminal possession of dangerous drugs, and criminal possession of drug paraphernalia. The district court denied his motion to suppress certain evidence and thereafter, defendant pled guilty to the offense of criminal manufacture of dangerous drugs. The remaining charges against him were dismissed. He appealed. The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part. The court found that the district court did not err in holding that probable cause existed for the issuance of the search warrant on the basis that unproven statements of a child information could not serve as the sole basis for the issuance of a search warrant. The court found that such statements could serve as the basis for the issuance of the search warrant. However, the court remanded the case to the district court to conduct a de novo hearing on defendant's motion to suppress, finding that it would have been inappropriate for the court to review the magistrate's determination that the application for the search warrant established probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part the denial of defendant's motion to suppress. The court found that it was inappropriate to review the magistrate's determination that the application for the search warrant established probable cause and remanded the case to conduct a de novo hearing on the motion to suppress.

Marshall v. State by & Through Cooney


No. 98-706


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 33; 293 Mont. 274; 975 P.2d 325; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 34; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 142


February 16, 1999, Argued and Submitted  
February 24, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Plaintiffs' request for reasonable attorneys fees and costs is denied. Secretary of State Cooney's motion to dismiss the claim filed against him is rendered moot by this decision.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed an original application for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief alleging a state constitutional initiative violated Mont. Const. art. XIV, § 11. Plaintiffs sought court costs and attorney fees and defendants moved to dismiss the claim.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged the constitutional validity of a state constitutional initiative that prohibited the enactment of a new tax or tax increase unless first approved by a majority of the electors voting on the measure in the geographic area subject to the tax. State voters approved the multi-part initiative. Plaintiffs filed an application for a declaratory judgment and sought a mandatory injunction directing defendants to decertify the election results and a permanent injunction prohibiting defendants from enforcing the provisions. Plaintiffs also sought court costs and attorney fees. Defendants responded that initiative was a valid constitutional amendment and moved to dismiss the claim. The court held the initiative expressly amended three parts of state constitution but did not allow for a separate vote for each amendment. Thus the initiative violated Mont. Const. art. XIV, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court held the tax initiative violated the state constitution since the initiative did not allow a separate vote for its amendments and objectionable parts could not be severed. Plaintiffs' request for attorneys' fees and costs was denied and defendants' motion to dismiss claim was rendered moot.

Roosevelt v. Montana Dep't of Revenue


No. 98-495


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1999 MT 30; 293 Mont. 240; 975 P.2d 295; 1999 Mont. LEXIS 32; 56 Mont. St. Rep. 125


December 29, 1998, Heard; February 2, 1999, Submitted  
February 19, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Tenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Fergus, The Honorable John Christensen, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the District Court affirmed in part and reversed in part, and remanded to the District Court for entry of judgment consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent department challenged the judgment of the District Court of the Tenth Judicial District, County of Fergus (Montana), which held that Mont. Code Ann. § 15-7-111(1) was unconstitutional on its face.


OVERVIEW: Respondent department applied a two percent phase-in on petitioner's property valuation pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 15-7-111(1). Petitioner contended the phase-in provision violated Mont. Const. art. III, § 3, which required the equalization of property values and the equal protection and due process laws guaranteed by the United States and Montana constitutions. The trial court agreed with petitioner and held the provision unconstitutional. Upon review, the court found that taxing petitioner at a percentage higher than the market value of his property, while taxing others in the state at less than full market value, was not rationally related to the legitimate state interest in reducing reliance on property taxes and avoiding further property tax increases. The court also held that the provision violated equal protection because it created a class of taxpayers who paid a disproportionate share of property taxes because their taxes were assessed on a basis greater than the market values of their properties. Because the provision did not adjust values over a short period of time and did not attain equality in tax treatment, it was unconstitutional as it applied to petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that the statutory phase-in was unconstitutional as it applied to petitioner because it deprived petitioner of the equal protection of the laws, but reversed the judgment insofar as it held that it was unconstitutional on its face.

DISPOSITION: District Court's sentencing order reversed and remanded for rehearing and resentencing consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, Cascade County (Montana) that sentenced him to, inter alia, ten years in prison for felony assault and an additional five years in prison for use of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with felony assault, Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-202(2)(b), and criminal trespass to property, Mont. Code Ann. § 45-6-203. A jury convicted appellant on all counts, and the trial court sentenced appellant to, inter alia, ten years in prison for felony assault and an additional five years in prison for use of a weapon pursuant to Mont. Const. art. II, § 25. The appellate court agreed and reversed the district court's sentencing order and remanded. When the weapon enhancement statute was applied to appellant's felony assault conviction, appellant was subjected to double punishment for use of a weapon.

Anderson v. Werner Enters., Inc.


No. 97-684


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 333; 292 Mont. 284; 972 P.2d 806; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 307; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 1350


April 30, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
December 30, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin, The Honorable Mike Salvagni, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, truck driver and employer, appealed from a jury verdict, judgment, and orders from the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin (Montana), in favor of plaintiff truck driver in plaintiff's suit for recovery of damages he sustained as a result of a three-vehicle accident.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff truck driver and defendant truck driver were involved in an accident as both drivers attempted to avoid a spinning car. Plaintiff truck driver was injured and sought recovery of damages. A claim between plaintiff and the driver of the car was settled. Judgment as a matter of law was entered as to liability and the jury awarded damages to plaintiff. Defendants, truck driver and owner, appealed. Defendants' argument that plaintiff's employment termination was grounds for reopening of discovery was not accepted. The court found that it was defendant's trial strategy that precluded rebuttal evidence from being developed. The court also rejected defendants' argument that the settling driver was subject to contribution. That party was properly dismissed upon settlement. The court affirmed judgment as a matter of law, because reasonable persons could have drawn no other conclusion but that the facts did not support a causal connection between plaintiff's action and his injuries. The court found no evidence of passion or prejudice in the jury award. Judgment for plaintiff was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment as a matter of law as to liability and a jury award of damages in favor of plaintiff truck driver was affirmed. No other conclusion but that plaintiff was not contributorily negligent could have been reached by a reasonable jury, and neither passion nor prejudice was considered in the jury award.

State v. Stanko


No. 98-106


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 323; 292 Mont. 214; 974 P.2d 1139; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 315; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 1313


August 20, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
December 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Tenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Fergus, The Honorable John R. Christensen, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the 10th Judicial District, Fergus County (Montana), which convicted defendant of two counts of reckless driving, Mont. Code Ann. § 46-13-401(2) violations. Defendant argued, among other things, that the six-month period under § 46-13-401(2) in which to try misdemeanors applied to a trial de novo in the district court and that Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-301 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged a district court's decision that convicted defendant of two counts of reckless driving, violations of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-13-401(2). Defendant contended, among other things, that § 46-13-401(2)'s six-month period applied to a trial de novo in the district court, that the district court erred in denying defendant's motion to dismiss, and that Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-301 was unconstitutionally vague as applied. The court affirmed the district court's decision. Defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated. Defendant failed to prove that he experienced anxiety or concern or that his defense was impaired in any way by the 216-day delay in reaching trial. The district court did not err in denying defendant's motion to dismiss based on defendant's argument that no one was injured and excessive speed could not be the sole basis for a reckless driving charge. There was sufficient evidence that defendant operated his vehicle in willful or wanton disregard for the safety of persons or property. Section 61-8-301 was not unconstitutionally vague because defendant did not show that he was unable to reasonably understand that his conduct was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a district court's decision that convicted defendant of two reckless driving counts. Because defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced, defendant's speedy trial right was not violated by a 216-day delay in reaching trial. Because defendant did not establish that he was reasonably unable to understand that his conduct was prohibited, the reckless driving statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

State v. Stanko


No. 97-486


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 321; 292 Mont. 192; 974 P.2d 1132; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 320; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 1302


October 14, 1998, Argued; November 17, 1998, Submitted  
December 23, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Sixteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Garfield, The Honorable Joe L. Hegel, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the District Court is reversed. Because we reverse the judgment of the District Court, we need not address the appellant's other argument regarding the assessment of costs and jury fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver appealed from the District Court of the Sixteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Garfield, Montana, his conviction for failing to drive in a reasonable and prudent manner in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-303(1).


OVERVIEW: After following defendant driver for a period of time, a police officer signaled for him to pull over and cited defendant for violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-303(1), which required a driver to drive in a careful and prudent manner and at a rate of speed no greater than is reasonable and proper under the conditions existing at the point of operation. Defendant appealed his conviction and contended that the statute was void for vagueness and violated the Due Process Clause, Mont. Const. Art. II, § 17. The reviewing court agreed and reversed his conviction. Defendant had standing to bring the action because his actions did not clearly prohibit the speed restriction of the statute in question. The court found that the statute impermissibly delegated the basic public policy of how fast is too fast on state highways to policemen, judges, and juries for arbitrary and discriminatory resolution. The court held that the statute did not define the crime with sufficient definiteness that ordinary people could understand what conduct was prohibited. Therefore, defendant's conviction was reversed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for speeding was reversed because the statute under which he was convicted was void for vagueness in violation of due process requirements.

 

33 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Woirhaye v. Montana Fourth Judicial Dist. Court


No. 98-223


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 320; 292 Mont. 185; 972 P.2d 800; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 333; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 1298


November 19, 1998, Heard and Submitted  
December 23, 1998, Decided



DISPOSITION:  We decline to follow the dicta in Hafdahl that the right to trial by jury is satisfied if it is granted at the district court level although denied at the small claims court level, and we will not follow the dicta in Hafdahl in future cases. We hold that because it impinges upon rights guaranteed under the Montana Constitution, § 46-17-201(3), MCA, is unconstitutional and therefore must be stricken from the laws of this State. For the same reason, the provisions of Chapter 129, L. 1997, which have been codified at §§ 46-7-102(1)(g) and 46-17-311(1), MCA, are stricken as well.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, misdemeanor criminal defendant, sought a writ of control regarding a decision of respondent district court that upheld the constitutionality of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-17-201(3). Relator argued that § 46-17-201(3) violated his right to trial by jury under Mont. Const. art. II, §§ 24 and 26 by allowing relator to exercise his right to a jury trial only once, in either justice court or in district court on trial de novo.


OVERVIEW: Relator, misdemeanor criminal defendant, sought a writ of control surrounding respondent district court's decision that upheld the constitutionality of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-17-201(3). Relator contended that § 46-17-201(3) violated his right to trial by jury pursuant to Mont. Const. art. II, §§ 24 and 26 by only allowing relator to exercise his right to a jury trial once, in either justice court or in district court on trial de novo. The court accepted jurisdiction and held that § 46-17-201(3) was unconstitutional because it impinged upon rights guaranteed under the state constitution. Trial de novo in district court was a different prosecution from one in justice court. Section 46-17-201(3) in effect forced waiver of the right to a jury trial either at the justice court level or at the district court level. Under the state constitution, a defendant had an absolute right not to be convicted of a misdemeanor by less than a unanimous jury. Section 46-17-201(3) unconstitutionally forced a misdemeanor defendant to be convicted by a judge, either in justice court or in a district court, rather than by a unanimous jury.


OUTCOME: The court held that a statute that allowed a misdemeanor criminal defendant to exercise his right to a jury trial once, in either justice court or in district court on trial de novo, was unconstitutional. The statute violated a misdemeanor criminal defendant's right to trial by jury under the state constitution.

 

34 of 930 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


No. 98-229


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 296N; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 280


October 22, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
December 3, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Tenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Fergus, The Honorable William Nels Swandal, Judge presiding.

Reported in table case format at: 1998 Mont. LEXIS 548.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, appearing pro se, appealed the bench trial judgment and sentencing order of the Tenth Judicial District Court, Fergus County (Montana), finding him guilty of driving without a valid driver's license under Mont. Code Ann. § 61-5-102, failure to exhibit proof of registration under Mont. Code Ann. § 61-3-322, and failure to exhibit proof of liability insurance under Mont. Code Ann. § 61-6-302.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the primary issues were: (1) whether the district court erred by conducting a bench trial without a written waiver of jury trial; (2) whether defendant was improperly sentenced for a dismissed charge; and (3) whether the motor vehicle codes denied defendant his constitutional freedom to travel or his right to due process of law. Under Mont. Const. art. II, § 26 and Mont. Code Ann. § 46-17-201, defendant's oral waiver of jury trial was valid. Defendant's second claim of error had no merit based on the record. Finally, the legislative enactments concerning the motor vehicle codes were presumed constitutional and would be upheld on review except when proven unconstitutional. The right to travel on public highways was not absolute and was subject to reasonable regulations by the state, including regulations on insurance coverage and registration, pursuant to the police power granted by the state constitution and there was no violation of defendant's due process rights under the United States Constitution. Finally, the caption on the sentencing order and judgment was not in any way inadequate because of a slight variation in defendant's middle name.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

35 of 930 DOCUMENTS


Dorwart v. Caraway


No. 95-446


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 191A; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 251



November 12, 1998, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditors challenged an order of the District Court of Stillwater County (Montana), which determined that Montana's post-judgment execution statutes were unconstitutional as applied because they did not provide the procedural due process of law required by Mont. Const. art. II, § 17, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: The creditors contested the trial court's finding that Montana's post-judgment execution statutes violated state and federal constitutional guarantees of due process of law. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) because the statutes did not provide for notice to a judgment debtor of the seizure of the debtor's property, of the availability of statutory exemptions from execution and where to locate additional information about them, and of the availability of procedures by which to claim exemptions from execution, the post-judgment execution statutes violated due process requirements; and (2) the statutes were also deficient from a due process standpoint because they did not provide for a prompt hearing on claimed exemptions.


OUTCOME: The court withdrew and replaced its earlier opinion and affirmed the trial court's holding that the post-judgment execution statutes were unconstitutional.

Ross v. City of Great Falls


No. 97-594


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 276; 291 Mont. 377; 967 P.2d 1103; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 254; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 1127


August 20, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
November 12, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, The Honorable Kenneth Neill, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of a decision of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Cascade County (Montana), which granted respondent city's motion for summary judgment and denied the applicant's motion for partial summary judgment on the issue of liability in the applicant's age discrimination action against the city stemming from her interest in applying to the city's police department for a police officer position.


OVERVIEW: The applicant was 37 years old when she received an application for a police officer position with the city's police department. The qualifications required that an applicant be between the ages of 18 and 35, as provided in Mont. Code Ann. § 7-32-4112(1) (1989), and the applicant filed a complaint with the state human rights commission, alleging age discrimination. Upon the recommendation of the commission, the applicant brought an action against the city under the Montana Human Rights Act (MHRA), Mont. Code Ann. tit. 49, ch. 2 and the Governmental Code of Fair Practices (GCFP), Mont. Code Ann. tit. 49, ch.3. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment and denied that of the applicant, and the applicant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that because the statute applied only to municipal police officers, it was not irreconcilably repugnant to the general prohibitions against age discrimination in the MHRA and the GCFP and thus the statute was not impliedly repealed by the enactment of the MHRA and the GCFP. The court found that even if the statute was unconstitutional, the city was immune from liability for acting in good faith reliance upon it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting the city's motion for summary judgment and denying the applicant's motion for partial summary judgment on the issue of liability in the applicant's age discrimination action against the city stemming from her interest in applying to the city's police department for a police officer position.

The court held that the foreign judgment that granted plaintiff a valid divorce was entitled to full faith and credit in Montana.

Girard v. Williams


No. 97-060


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 231; 291 Mont. 49; 966 P.2d 1155; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 214; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 965


October 9, 1997, Argued; October 30, 1997, Submitted  
September 15, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 29, 1998. Released for Publication November 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, In and for the County of Ravalli, The Honorable John W. Larson, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant biological father sought review of a decision of the District Court of the 21st Judicial District in and for the County of Ravalli (Montana), which awarded permanent custody of the biological father's minor children to intervenor relatives.


OVERVIEW: The children were living with their mother in Arizona. Upon her death, the children were transported to Montana to live with their putative father's relatives, as putative father was incarcerated at the time. After his release from prison, the putative father filed a petition to gain custody of the children. The biological father, who had also been incarcerated for a period of time, appeared in the proceeding to challenge the putative father's claim that it was in the children's best interest that he be granted sole and permanent custody. During the pendency of the proceeding, the putative father died and the trial court permitted the relatives to intervene to seek custody of the children. The trial court subsequently granted permanent custody to the relatives. The court held that (1) the matter was governed by the Uniform Marriage and Divorce Act (UMDA), specifically Mont. Code Ann. § 40-4; (2) the relatives did not have standing to intervene under the UMDA because they failed to show that the biological father voluntarily relinquished his right to custody of the children; and (3) the biological father's period of incarceration did not constitute voluntary relinquishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the matter with instructions for the trial court to grant custody of the children to the biological father.

State v. Clark


No. 97-096


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 221; 290 Mont. 479; 964 P.2d 766; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 200; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 919


April 27, 1998, Heard; April 30, 1998, Submitted  
September 3, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin, The Honorable Thomas A. Olson, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded to the District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Gallatin, Montana, which convicted defendant of various criminal offenses after permitting the introduction into evidence of a state's crime lab report as an exception to the hearsay rule, under Mont. R. Evid. 803(8).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal possession of dangerous drugs and drug paraphernalia, driving under the influence of alcohol, failure to remain at the scene of an accident, and failure of duty upon striking an unattended vehicle. The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded for a new trial. The court held that Mont. R. Evid. 803(8), which provided an exception to the hearsay rule for written reports from the Montana state crime laboratory, violated Mont. Const. art. II, § 24, and the due process clause guarantees embodied in Mont. Const. art. II, § 17. The court held that Mont. R. Evid. 803(8) deprived defendant of an opportunity to cross-exam the lab technician and impermissibly shifted the burden of producing the prosecution's experts to defendant. However, the court held that the prosecution's amendment of the information, which changed the nature of the drug possessed by defendant, was proper because it was an amendment of form only.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions of criminal possession of dangerous drugs and drug paraphernalia, driving under the influence of alcohol, failure to remain at the scene of an accident, and failure of duty upon striking an unattended vehicle, and remanded for a new trial.

Dorwart v. Caraway


No. 95-446


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


1998 MT 191; 290 Mont. 196; 966 P.2d 1121; 1998 Mont. LEXIS 172; 55 Mont. St. Rep. 777


June 12, 1997, Argued; July 15, 1997, Submitted  
August 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 12, 1998. Released for Publication November 12, 1998. Certiorari Denied April 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2369.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Stillwater, The Honorable Maurice R. Colberg, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judgment debtor challenged an order from the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District (Montana), which granted partial summary judgment to defendants, county and officials, in plaintiff's action alleging violations of his U.S. Const. amend. IV and Mont. Const. art. II, § 10 rights. Defendants challenged a partial summary judgment for the judgment debtor finding Montana post-judgment execution statutes unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a writ of execution against the judgment debtor, county officials entered the debtor's residence without his permission and levied upon his personal property, at least some of which was exempt. The judgment debtor filed an action against the county and the officials, alleging, inter alia, that his U.S. Const. amend IV and Mont. Const. art. II, §811 rights were violated. On appeal, the court ruled that the district court erred in determining that the officials' actions did not violate his constitutional rights against unreasonable search and seizure because the debtor had an expectation of privacy and there were no exigent circumstances. The court then applied the Mathews three-part balancing test to determine that the Montana post-judgment execution statutes were unconstitutional because they did not provide for proper notice and a hearing to a judgment debtor. The court also ruled that the district court properly granted summary judgment as to the debtor's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 actions because the officials were entitled to qualified immunity since it was not clearly established at the time that a writ of execution did not authorize them to enter the debtor's residence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, reversing and remanding as to the partial summary judgment granted to defendants on the judgment creditor's action alleging violations of his constitutional rights to be free from unreasonable search and seizure. The court affirmed as to the findings that Montana post-judgment execution statutes were unconstitutional and that the officials were entitled to qualified immunity.

City of Billings v. Bruce

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Yellowstone, The Honorable Maurice R. Colberg, Jr., Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, Yellowstone County (Montana), which denied his motion to dismiss stalking charges against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the offense of stalking in the city court. He appealed and filed motions to dismiss the charges on the ground that his rights to a speedy trial and due process were violated. The district court denied these motions. Defendant sought review and asserted that he was denied his right to a speedy trial in the district and city courts and the charging instrument in the city court failed to provide adequate notice. The state asserted that defendant failed give notice of his desire for a speedy trial. The court held that: (1) defendant timely asserted his right to a speedy trial because he filed a motion to dismiss on speedy trial grounds prior to the time of trial, (2) the length of delay from the time of appeal to the date of trial was sufficient to trigger the speedy trial analysis, (3) the delay in the trial was attributable to the city, and (4) and the city failed to rebut the presumption that defendant's defense was impaired.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges of stalking.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant individuals appeal the denial of their motion to set aside a default and default judgment entered by the District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, In and for the County of Toole (Montana), in an action brought by plaintiff department of environmental quality (DEQ). Their motion was deemed denied by operation of law when the district court failed to rule on it within 60 days as provided for by Mont. R. Civ. P. 60(c).

The individuals maintained that the DEQ misled them into believing that there would not be a default judgment as long as they cooperated with the DEQ in bringing their facility into compliance. The individuals believed that they cooperated with the DEQ. The court held that the individuals did not appear in the action and did not present a meritorious defense to the DEQ's cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of a default judgment against the individuals in the action brought by the DEQ. The district court did not err in failing to set aside the default judgment and entry of default.
